Tourism</a> (in Spanish)</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sabana_de_Bogota.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="902" data-file-width="1068" decoding="async" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sabana_de_Bogota.png/340px-Sabana_de_Bogota.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sabana_de_Bogota.png/510px-Sabana_de_Bogota.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sabana_de_Bogota.png/680px-Sabana_de_Bogota.png 2x" width="340"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sabana_de_Bogota.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bogot&#225; savanna is the high plateau in the Andes where Bogot&#225; is located. The flatlands are clearly visible in the topography and the result of a <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> lake; Lake Humboldt, that existed until around 30,000 years BP</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Bogot&#225;</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/o&#650;/: \'o\' in \'code\'">o&#650;</span><span title="/&#609;/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">&#609;</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#716;/: secondary stress follows">&#716;</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/&#594;/: \'o\' in \'body\'">&#594;</span><span title="/&#609;/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">&#609;</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#716;/: secondary stress follows">&#716;</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/o&#650;/: \'o\' in \'code\'">o&#650;</span></span>-/</a></span></span>; <small>Spanish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[bo&#611;o&#712;ta]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ca/Bogot%C3%A1.ogg" title="Bogot&#225;.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), officially <b>Bogot&#225;, Distrito Capital</b>, abbreviated <b>Bogot&#225;, D.C.</b>, and formerly known as <b>Santaf&#233;/Santa F&#233; de Bogot&#225;</b> between 1991 and 2000, is the capital and largest city of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, administered as the Capital District, although often erroneously thought of as part of <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department" title="Cundinamarca Department">Cundinamarca</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Bogot&#225; is a territorial entity of the first order, with the same administrative status as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_(Colombia)" title="Department (Colombia)">departments of Colombia</a>. It is the political, economic, administrative, industrial, artistic, cultural, and sports center of the country.\n</p><p>Bogot&#225; was founded as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Kingdom of Granada</a> on August 6, 1538, by Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada</a> after a harsh <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">expedition into the Andes conquering the Muisca</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muisca_people" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a> were the indigenous inhabitants of the region and called the settlement where Bogot&#225; was founded <i><a href="/wiki/Bacat%C3%A1" title="Bacat&#225;">Bacat&#225;</a></i>, which in the Chibcha language means "The Lady of the Andes." Further, the word \'Andes\' in the Aymara language means "shining mountain," thus rendering the full lexical signification of Bogot&#225; as "The Lady of the shining mountain." After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Boyac%C3%A1" title="Battle of Boyac&#225;">Battle of Boyac&#225;</a> on August 7, 1819, Bogot&#225; became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Colombian Declaration of Independence">independent</a> nation of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a>. Since the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>\'s independence from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and during the formation of present-day Colombia, Bogot&#225; has remained the capital of this territory.\n</p><p>The city is located in the center of Colombia, on a high plateau known as the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_savanna" title="Bogot&#225; savanna">Bogot&#225; savanna</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Altiplano_Cundiboyacense" title="Altiplano Cundiboyacense">Altiplano Cundiboyacense</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Oriental (Colombia)">Eastern Cordillera</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>. It is the third-highest capital in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and in the world after <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>, at an average of 2,640 metres (8,660&#160;ft) above sea level. Subdivided into 20 localities, Bogot&#225; has an area of 1,587 square kilometres (613 square miles) and a relatively cool climate that is constant through the year.\n</p><p>The city is home to central offices of the executive branch (<a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic" title="President of the Republic">Office of the President</a>), the legislative branch (<a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Colombia" title="Congress of Colombia">Congress of Colombia</a>) and the judicial branch (<a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_of_Colombia" title="Supreme Court of Justice of Colombia">Supreme Court of Justice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Colombia" title="Constitutional Court of Colombia">Constitutional Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_(Colombia)" title="Council of State (Colombia)">Council of State</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Superior_Council_of_Judicature" title="Superior Council of Judicature">Superior Council of Judicature</a>) of the Colombian government. Bogot&#225; stands out for its economic strength and associated financial maturity, its attractiveness to global companies and the quality of human capital. It is the financial and commercial heart of Colombia, with the most business activity of any city in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hotspots_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hotspots-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheTalentIssue_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheTalentIssue-14">[14]</a></sup> The capital hosts the main financial market in Colombia and the <a href="/wiki/Andean_natural_region" title="Andean natural region">Andean natural region</a>, and is the leading destination for new foreign direct investment projects coming into Latin America and Colombia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-investmentIBM_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-investmentIBM-15">[15]</a></sup> It has the highest nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> in the country, responsible for almost a quarter of the nation\'s total (24.7%).\n</p><p>The city\'s airport, <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a>, named after the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_mythology" title="Muisca mythology">mythical</a> <i><a href="/wiki/El_Dorado" title="El Dorado">El Dorado</a></i>, handles the largest cargo volume in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, and is third in number of people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Bogot&#225; is home to the largest number of universities and research centers in the country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheTalentIssue_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-TheTalentIssue-14">[14]</a></sup> and is an important cultural center, with many theaters, libraries and museums, of which the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Gold Museum, Bogot&#225;">Museo del Oro</a> is the most important,. Bogot&#225; ranks 52nd on the Global Cities Index 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and is considered a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> type "Alpha &#8722;" by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GaWC" title="GaWC">GaWC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div Bogot&#225;</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-50"><a href="#Pre-Muisca"><span class="tocnumber">18.1</span> <span class="toctext">Pre-Muisca</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-51"><a href="#Economy_2"><span class="tocnumber">18.2</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-52"><a href="#Society_&amp;_tunjos"><span tocsection-56"><a href="#Mythology_and_religion"><span class="tocnumber">18.7</span> <span class="toctext">Mythology and religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-57"><a href="#Women_in_early_colonial_Bogot&#225;"><span class="tocnumber">18.8</span> <span class="toctext">Women in early colonial Bogot&#225;</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-58"><a href="#Early_colonial_Muisca"><span class="tocnumber">18.9</span> <span class="toctext">Early colonial Muisca</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-59"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="History of Bogot&#225;">History of Bogot&#225;</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Bogot%C3%A1_history" title="Timeline of Bogot&#225; history">Timeline of Bogot&#225; history</a></div>\n<p>The area of modern Bogot&#225; was first populated by groups of indigenous people who migrated south based on the relation with the other Chibcha languages; the Bogot&#225; savanna was the southernmost Chibcha-speaking group that exists from Nicaragua to the Andes in Colombia. The civilisation built by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muisca_people" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a>, who settled in the valleys and fertile highlands of and surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Altiplano_Cundiboyacense" title="Altiplano Cundiboyacense">Altiplano Cundiboyacense</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Colombia" title="Departments of Colombia">departments</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department" title="Cundinamarca Department">Cundinamarca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boyac%C3%A1_Department" title="Boyac&#225; Department">Boyac&#225;</a> and small parts of <a href="/wiki/Santander_Department" title="Santander Department">Santander</a>), was one of the four great civilisations in the Americas. The name <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a> has been given to a loose egalitarian society of various chiefs (<i>caciques</i>) who lived in small settlements of maximum 100 <i><a href="/wiki/Muisca_architecture" title="Muisca architecture">boh&#237;os</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_agriculture" title="Muisca agriculture">agriculture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muisca_economy#Salt" title="Muisca economy">salt-based</a> society of the people was rich in goldworking, <a href="/wiki/Muisca_economy#Trade" title="Muisca economy">trade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muisca_mummification" title="Muisca mummification">mummification</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_religion" title="Muisca religion">religion</a> of the Muisca consisted of various gods, mostly related to natural phenomena as the Sun (<a href="/wiki/Su%C3%A9" title="Su&#233;">Su&#233;</a>) and his wife, the Moon; <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%ADa_(goddess)" title="Ch&#237;a (goddess)">Ch&#237;a</a>, rain <a href="/wiki/Chibchacum" title="Chibchacum">Chibchacum</a>, rainbow <a href="/wiki/Cuchavira" title="Cuchavira">Cuchavira</a> and with building and feasting (<a href="/wiki/Nencatacoa" title="Nencatacoa">Nencatacoa</a>) and wisdom (<a href="/wiki/Bochica" title="Bochica">Bochica</a>). Their complex <a href="/wiki/Muisca_calendar" title="Muisca calendar">luni-solar calendar</a>, deciphered by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Arturo_Izquierdo_Pe%C3%B1a" title="Manuel Arturo Izquierdo Pe&#241;a">Manuel Izquierdo</a> based on work by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Domingo_Duquesne" title="Jos&#233; Domingo Duquesne">Duquesne</a>, followed three different sets of years, where the <a href="/wiki/Sidereal_year" title="Sidereal year">sidereal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synodic" title="Synodic">synodic</a> months were represented. Their <a href="/wiki/Muisca_astronomy" title="Muisca astronomy">astronomical knowledge</a> is represented in one of the few extant landmarks of the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_architecture" title="Muisca architecture">architecture</a> of the Muisca in <i><a href="/wiki/El_Infiernito" title="El Infiernito">El Infiernito</a></i> outside <a href="/wiki/Villa_de_Leyva" title="Villa de Leyva">Villa de Leyva</a> to the north of Bogot&#225;.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_era">Pre-Columbian era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" Period">Herrera Period</a></div>\n<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks hlist" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid people">Muzo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Panche_people" title="Panche people">Panche</a></li></ul></td>\n</tr><tr><th style="padding:0.1em">\n<a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_the_Muisca" Cundiboyacense">timeline</a></th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation#Prehistory" title="Muisca Confederation">Prehistory</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Herrera_Period" title="Herrera Period">Herrera Period</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Bacat&#225;</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tunja" title="Tunja">Hunza</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sogamoso" title="Sogamoso">Suamox</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Duitama" title="Duitama">Tundama</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">Spanish conquest</a>\n<ul><li><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada">Gonzalo</a></span></li>\n<li><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_P%C3%A9rez_de_Quesada" title="Hern&#225;n P&#233;rez de Quesada">Hern&#225;n</a></span></li>\n<li><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/List_of_conquistadors_in_Colombia" title="List of conquistadors in Colombia">Others</a></span></li></ul></li></ul></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Muisca_sidebar" title="Template:Muisca sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Muisca_sidebar" title="Template talk:Muisca sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Muisca_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="775" data-file-width="531" decoding="async" height="336" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG/230px-Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG/345px-Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG/460px-Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Don_Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada</a>, founder of the city</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chorro_quevedo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chorro_quevedo.jpg/230px-Chorro_quevedo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chorro_quevedo.jpg/345px-Chorro_quevedo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chorro_quevedo.jpg/460px-Chorro_quevedo.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chorro_quevedo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The fountain of Quevedo on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chorro_de_Quevedo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chorro de Quevedo (page does not exist)">Chorro de Quevedo</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorro_de_Quevedo" title="es:Chorro de Quevedo">es</a>]</span>, one of the possible foundation sites of Bogot&#225;</div></div></div>\n<p>The first populations inhabiting the present-day <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Area_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Metropolitan Area of Bogot&#225;">Metropolitan Area of Bogot&#225;</a>, were hunter-gatherer people in the late Pleistocene. The oldest dated evidence thus far has been discovered in <i><a href="/wiki/El_Abra" title="El Abra">El Abra</a></i> (12,500 BP), north of <a href="/wiki/Zipaquir%C3%A1" title="Zipaquir&#225;">Zipaquir&#225;</a>. Slightly later dated excavations in a rock shelter southwest of the city in <a href="/wiki/Soacha" title="Soacha">Soacha</a> provided ages of ~11,000 <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">BP</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tequendama" title="Tequendama">Tequendama</a>. Since around 0 AD, the Muisca domesticated <a href="/wiki/Guinea_pig" title="Guinea pig">guinea pigs</a>, part of their meat diet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The people inhabiting the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_savanna" title="Bogot&#225; savanna">Bogot&#225; savanna</a> in the late 15th century were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muisca_people" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a>, speaking <i><a href="/wiki/Chibcha_language" title="Chibcha language">Muysccubun</a></i>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Chibcha_language#Comparison_to_other_Chibchan_languages" title="Chibcha language">Chibcha</a> language family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElCarnero_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-ElCarnero-20">[20]</a></sup> Muisca means "people" or "person", making "Muisca people", how they are called, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tautology_(grammar)" title="Tautology (grammar)">tautology</a>. At the arrival of the conquerors, the population was estimated to be half a million indigenous people on the Bogot&#225; savanna of up to two million in the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a>. They occupied the highland and mild climate flanks between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumapaz_Paramo" title="Sumapaz Paramo">Sumapaz Mountains</a> to the southwest and Cocuy\'s snowy peak to the northeast, covering an approximate area of 25,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (9,653&#160;sq&#160;mi), comprising Bogot&#225;\'s high plain, the current <a href="/wiki/Boyac%C3%A1_Department" title="Boyac&#225; Department">Boyac&#225;</a> department portion and a small <a href="/wiki/Santander_Department" title="Santander Department">Santander</a> region.\n</p><p>Trade was the most important activity of the Muisca with other Chibcha-speaking neighbours,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> such as the <a href="/wiki/Guane_people" title="Guane people">Guane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lache_people" title="Lache people">Lache</a> and <a href="/wiki/U%27wa_people" title="U\'wa people">U\'wa</a> and with Cariban groups as the <a href="/wiki/Muzo_people" title="Muzo people">Muzo</a> or "Emerald People". Their knowledge of salt production from brines, a task exclusively for the <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Muisca_society" title="Women in Muisca society">Muisca women</a>, gave them the name "Salt People".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daza_2728_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Daza_2728-22">[22]</a></sup> Tropical fruits that didn\'t grow on the cool highlands, <a href="/wiki/Coca" title="Coca">coca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> were traded at markets that took place every Muisca week; every four days. At these frequent markets, the Muisca obtained various luxury goods that seem worthless in modern sense and precious metals and gemstones that seem valuable to us became abundant and used for various purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_warfare" title="Muisca warfare">Muisca warrior elite</a> was allowed to wear feathered crowns, from parrots and macacs whose habitat was to the east of the Andes; the <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawkan</a>-speaking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayupe_people" title="Guayupe people">Guayupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tegua_people" title="Tegua people">Tegua</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Achagua_people" title="Achagua people">Achagua</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_cuisine" title="Muisca cuisine">Muisca cuisine</a> consisted of a stable and varied diet of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tubers" title="Tubers">tubers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a> and fruits. <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Maize</a> was the main ingredient of the Muisca, cultivated on <a href="/wiki/Muisca_agriculture" title="Muisca agriculture">elevated and irrigated terraces</a>. In Muysccubun exist many words for <i>maize</i>, <i>corn</i> and <a href="/wiki/Muisca_cuisine" title="Muisca cuisine">the various types and forms of it</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daza_2728_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Daza_2728-22">[22]</a></sup> The product was also the base for <a href="/wiki/Chicha#Colombia" title="Chicha">chicha</a>; the alcoholic beverage of the people, still sold in central Bogot&#225; today. It was the drink for construction of houses, celebrations of harvests and sowing, ritual practices around the various sacred sites of the Altiplano, <a href="/wiki/Muisca_music" title="Muisca music">music and dances</a>, trade at special ferias with farther away trading indigenous groups of Colombia and to inaugurate the new highest regarded member of the community; <i>zipas</i>, <i>zaques</i>, <i>caciques</i> and the religious ruler <i><a href="/wiki/Iraca" title="Iraca">iraca</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Sun_Temple_(Sogamoso)" title="Sun Temple (Sogamoso)">Sacred City of the Sun</a> <a href="/wiki/Sogamoso" title="Sogamoso">Sugamuxi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>zipa</i> at the moment of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">Spanish conquest</a> was <a href="/wiki/Tisquesusa" title="Tisquesusa">Tisquesusa</a>. His main <i>boh&#237;o</i> was in <i>Bacat&#225;</i> with others in <a href="/wiki/Funza" title="Funza">Funza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cajic%C3%A1" title="Cajic&#225;">Cajic&#225;</a>, giving name to the present day capital of Colombia. A prophecy in his life came true; <i>he would be dying, bathing in his own blood</i>. Defending Funza with a reduced army of <a href="/wiki/Muisca_warfare" title="Muisca warfare">guecha warriors</a> against the heavily exhausted but heavily armed strangers, his reign fell in the hands of Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada and his younger brother <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_P%C3%A9rez_de_Quesada" title="Hern&#225;n P&#233;rez de Quesada">Hern&#225;n P&#233;rez</a> on April 20, 1537. Upon his death, his brother <a href="/wiki/Sagipa" title="Sagipa">Sagipa</a> became the last <i>zipa</i>, against the <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Muisca_society" title="Women in Muisca society">inheritance tradition of the Muisca</a>. Sagipa used to be a main captain for Tisquesusa but quickly submitted to the Spanish rulers. The first <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomenderos</a> asked high prices in valuable products and agricultural production from the indigenous people. On top of that  epidemics of European viruses razed through the population, of which in current <a href="/wiki/Boyac%C3%A1_Department" title="Boyac&#225; Department">Boyac&#225;</a> 65&#8211;85&#160;% of the Muisca were killed within 100 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bogot&#225; was founded by <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada</a> traditionally on the 6th of August 1538. Other documents state a second establishment was done on April 27, 1539. Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez and main conquerors <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_Belalc%C3%A1zar" title="Sebasti&#225;n de Belalc&#225;zar">De Belalc&#225;zar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikolaus_Federmann" title="Nikolaus Federmann">Federmann</a>, left for Spain in April 1539, founding <a href="/wiki/Guataqu%C3%AD" title="Guataqu&#237;">Guataqu&#237;</a> together on April 6, 1539. The rule over the fresh <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Kingdom of Granada</a> was left to Hern&#225;n. The first mayors of the city were capitains <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pedro_de_Arevalo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pedro de Arevalo (page does not exist)">Pedro de Arevalo</a> y <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jeronimo_de_Inzar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jeronimo de Inzar (page does not exist)">Jeronimo de Inzar</a>. Bogot&#225; became the capital of the later <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElCarnero_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-ElCarnero-20">[20]</a></sup> With independence, Bogot&#225; became capital of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a> and later the capital of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Colombia" title="Republic of Colombia">Republic of Colombia</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Gonzalo_Jim.C3.A9nez_de_Quesada_expedition"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gonzalo_Jim&#233;nez_de_Quesada_expedition">Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada expedition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada expedition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">Spanish conquest of the Muisca</a></div>\n<p>From 1533, a belief persisted that the R&#237;o Grande de la <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena</a> was the trail to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">South Sea</a>, to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Per%C3%BA" title="Per&#250;">Per&#250;</a>, legendary <i><a href="/wiki/El_Dorado" title="El Dorado">El Dorado</a></i>. Such was the target of <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jim&#233;nez de Quesada</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Granada" title="Kingdom of Granada">Granadanian</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_conquistadors_in_Colombia" title="List of conquistadors in Colombia">conquistador</a> who left <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a> on 6 April 1536 with 800 soldiers, heading towards the interior of current <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>. The expedition divided into two groups, one under Quesada\'s command to move on land, and the other commanded by Diego de Urbino would go up river in four brigantine ships to, later on, meet Quesada troops at the site named Tora de las Barrancas Bermejas. When they arrived, they heard news about Indians inhabiting the south and making large salt cakes used to trade for wild cotton and fish. Jim&#233;nez decided to abandon the route to <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and cross the mountain in search of salt villages. They saw crops, trails, white salt cakes and then huts where they found corn, yucca and beans. From Tora, the expedition went up the Op&#243;n River and found indigenous people covered with very finely painted cotton mantles. When they arrived in Muisca territories, of the expedition leaving <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a>, only 162 men were left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BancoList_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-BancoList-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_colonization">Spanish colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spanish colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On the other side to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bol&#237;var Square">Plaza de Bol&#237;var</a>, the Chapter and the Royal Audience were located. The street joining the Major Plaza and Herbs Plaza &#8212; Santander Park&#8212; was named <i>Calle Real</i> (Royal Street), now <i>Carrera S&#233;ptima</i> (or "Seventh Street"; counted from the mountains to the east of the city).\n</p><p>Formed by Europeans, <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a>, indigenous people, and slaves, from the second half of the 16th century, the population began to grow rapidly. The 1789 census recorded 18,161 inhabitants, and by 1819 the city population reached 30,000 inhabitants distributed in 195 blocks. Importance grew when the <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">Diocese</a> was established.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The city mayor and the chapter formed by two councilmen, assisted by the constable and the police chief, governed the city. For better administration of these domains, in April 1550, the Audience of Santaf&#233; de Bogot&#225; was organized. At that time, the city became the capital and the home of New Kingdom of Granada government. Fourteen years later in 1564, the Spanish Crown designated the first Royal Audience chairman, Andr&#233;s D&#237;az Venero de Leyva.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nineteenth_century">Nineteenth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nineteenth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg/230px-CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg/345px-CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg/460px-CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bol&#237;var Square">Bol&#237;var Square</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="1228" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg/230px-Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg/345px-Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg/460px-Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Royal Street, today known as the Seventh Avenue (Carrera S&#233;ptima)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1644" data-file-width="3338" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg/230px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg/345px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg/460px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Sabana_2010_retusche.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bogot&#225;\'s Railroad Central Station</div></div></div>\n<p>Political unease felt all over Spanish colonies in America was expressed in New Granada in many different ways, accelerating the movement to independence. One of the most transcendent was the Revolution of Comuneros, a riot of the inhabitants started in Villa del Socorro &#8212;current Department of <a href="/wiki/Santander_Department" title="Santander Department">Santander</a>&#8212;in March 1781.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Spanish authorities suppressed the riot, and Jos&#233; Antonio Gal&#225;n, the leader, was executed. He left an imprint, though. He was followed in 1794 by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Nari%C3%B1o" title="Antonio Nari&#241;o">Antonio Nari&#241;o</a>, precursor of independence by translating and publishing in Santa Fe, the Rights of Men and the Citizen, and by 20 July movement leaders in 1810.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Between 1819 and 1849, there were no fundamental structural changes from the colonial period. By the mid-19th century, a series of fundamental reforms were enacted, some of the most important being slavery abolition and religious, teaching, print and speech industry and trade freedom, among others.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> During the decade of the 70s, radicalism accelerated reforms and state and social institutions were substantially modified. However, during the second half of the century, the country faced permanent pronouncements, declarations of rebellions between states, and factions which resulted in civil wars: the last and bloodiest was the <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Days%27_War" title="Thousand Days\' War">Thousand Days\' War</a> from 1899 to 1902.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>In 1823, a few years after the formation of Gran Colombia, the Public Library, now the National Library, was enlarged and modernized with new volumes and better facilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The National Museum was founded. Those institutions were of great importance to the new republic\'s cultural development.  The Central University was the first State school, precursor of the current <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia" title="National University of Colombia">National University</a>, founded in 1867 and domiciled in Bogot&#225;.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regeneration">Regeneration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Regeneration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>President Rafael N&#250;&#241;ez declared the end of Federalism, and in 1886 the country became a centralist republic ruled by the constitution in force &#8211; save some amendments &#8211; up to 1981. In the middle of political and administration avatars, Bogot&#225; continued as the capital and principal political center of the country.\n</p><p>From a base of only 20,000 people in 1793, the city grew to approximately 117,000 people in 1912. Population growth was rapid after 1870, largely because of emigration from the eastern highlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twentieth_century">Twentieth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Twentieth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Early in the 20th century, Colombia had to face devastating consequences from the One Thousand Days War, which lasted from 1899 to 1902, and the loss of <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Between 1904 and 1909, the lawfulness of the liberal party was re-established and President Rafael Reyes endeavored to implement a national government. Peace and state reorganization generated the increase of economic activities. Bogot&#225; started deep architectural and urban transformation with significant industrial and artisan production increases.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1910, the Industrial Exposition of the Century took place at Park of Independence. Stands built evidenced industrial, artisan work, beaux arts, electricity and machinery progress achieved. The period from 1910 to 1930 is designated conservative hegemony.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Between 1924 and 1928, hard union struggles began, with oil fields and banana zone workers\' strikes, leaving numerous people dead.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Bogot&#225; had practically no industry. Production was basically artisan work grouped in specific places, similar to commercial sectors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bol&#237;var Square">Plaza de Bol&#237;var</a> and surroundings lodged hat stores, at Calle del Comercio &#8211;current Carrera Seventh&#8211; and Calle Flori&#225;n &#8211;now Carrera Eight&#8211; luxurious stores selling imported products opened their doors; at Pasaje Hern&#225;ndez, tailor\'s shops provided their services, and between 1870 and 1883, four main banks opened their doors: Bogot&#225;, Colombia, Popular and Mortgage Credit banks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bogotazo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="244" data-file-width="391" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg/220px-Bogotazo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg/330px-Bogotazo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bogotazo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bogotazo</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bogotazo" title="Bogotazo">Bogotazo</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Violencia" title="La Violencia">La Violencia</a></div>\n<p>Following the banana zone killings and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Conservative_Party" title="Colombian Conservative Party">conservative party</a> division, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Olaya_Herrera" title="Enrique Olaya Herrera">Enrique Olaya Herrera</a> took office in 1930. The <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Liberal_Party" title="Colombian Liberal Party">liberal party</a> reformed during 16 years of the so-called Liberal Republic, agricultural, social, political, labor, educational, economic and administrative sectors. Unionism strengthened and education coverage expanded.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The celebration produced a large number of infrastructure works, new construction and work sources. Following the 1946 liberal party division, a conservative candidate took presidential office again in 1948, after the killing of liberal leader <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Eli%C3%A9cer_Gait%C3%A1n" title="Jorge Eli&#233;cer Gait&#225;n">Jorge Eli&#233;cer Gait&#225;n</a>, Bogot&#225;\'s downtown was virtually destroyed as violence reigned. From then, Bogot&#225;\'s urban, architectural and population sectors were substantially reorganized.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty-first_century">Twenty-first century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Twenty-first century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg/300px-Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg/450px-Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg/600px-Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mira_a_lo_alto.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bogot&#225; is the third largest city within city limits in South America by population, after <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="S&#227;o Paulo">S&#227;o Paulo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a></div></div></div>\n<table class="box-Empty_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section is empty.</b> <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2016</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg/220px-Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg/330px-Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg/440px-Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sumapaz_P%C3%A1ramo" title="Sumapaz P&#225;ramo">Sumapaz P&#225;ramo</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG/220px-Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG/330px-Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG/440px-Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eastern Hills</div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225; is located in the southeastern part of the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_savanna" title="Bogot&#225; savanna">Bogot&#225; savanna</a> (<i>Sabana de Bogot&#225;</i>) at an average altitude of 2,640 metres (8,660&#160;ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alcaldia_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Alcaldia-7">[7]</a></sup> The Bogot&#225; savanna is popularly called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savannah" title="Savannah">savannah</a>" (<i>sabana</i>), but constitutes actually a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_plateau" title="High plateau">high plateau</a> in the Andes mountains, part of an extended region known as the <a href="/wiki/Altiplano_Cundiboyacense" title="Altiplano Cundiboyacense">Altiplano Cundiboyacense</a>, which literally means "high plateau of Cundinamarca and Boyac&#225;".\n</p><p>In the extreme south of Bogota\'s District, the world\'s largest continuous <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1ramo" title="P&#225;ramo">paramo</a> ecosystem can be found; <a href="/wiki/Sumapaz_P%C3%A1ramo" title="Sumapaz P&#225;ramo">Sumapaz P&#225;ramo</a> in the locality <a href="/wiki/Sumapaz" title="Sumapaz">Sumapaz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_River" title="Bogot&#225; River">Bogot&#225; River</a> running NE-SW crosses the <i>sabana</i>, forming <a href="/wiki/Tequendama_Falls" title="Tequendama Falls">Tequendama Falls</a> (<i>Salto del Tequendama</i>) to the south. Tributary rivers form valleys with flourishing villages, whose economy is based on agriculture, livestock raising and artisanal production.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The <i>sabana</i> is bordered to the east by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental,_Colombia" title="Cordillera Oriental, Colombia">Eastern Cordillera</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> mountain range. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Hills_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Eastern Hills (Bogot&#225;)">Eastern Hills</a>, which limit city growth, run from south to north, and form east of the center the Guadalupe and <a href="/wiki/Monserrate" title="Monserrate">Monserrate</a> mountains. The western city limit is the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_River" title="Bogot&#225; River">Bogot&#225; River</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumapaz_Paramo" title="Sumapaz Paramo">Sumapaz Paramo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a>) borders the south and to the north Bogot&#225; extends over the plateau up to the towns of <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%ADa,_Cundinamarca" title="Ch&#237;a, Cundinamarca">Ch&#237;a</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sop%C3%B3" title="Sop&#243;">Sop&#243;</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hail_in_Bogota.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="603" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Hail_in_Bogota.jpg/220px-Hail_in_Bogota.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Hail_in_Bogota.jpg/330px-Hail_in_Bogota.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Hail_in_Bogota.jpg/440px-Hail_in_Bogota.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hail_in_Bogota.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">Hailstorm</a> in Bogot&#225;</div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225; has a <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">subtropical highland</a> climate (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen</a> <i>Cfb</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate-Data.org_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-Data.org-29">[29]</a></sup> The average temperature is 14.5&#160;&#176;C (58&#160;&#176;F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> varying from 6 to 19&#160;&#176;C (43 to 66&#160;&#176;F) on sunny days to 10 to 18&#160;&#176;C (50 to 64&#160;&#176;F) on rainy days. Dry and rainy seasons alternate throughout the year. The driest months are December, January, July and August. The warmest month is March, bringing a maximum of 19.7&#160;&#176;C (67.5&#160;&#176;F). The coolest nights occur in January, with an average of 7.6&#160;&#176;C (45.7&#160;&#176;F) in the city; fog is very usual in early morning, 220 days per year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS-31">[31]</a></sup> whilst clear sky sunny full days are quite unusual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The official highest temperature recorded within the city limits is 30.0&#160;&#176;C (86&#160;&#176;F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-climate-32">[32]</a></sup> and the lowest temperature recorded is &#8722;7.1&#160;&#176;C (19&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-climate-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rainiest months are April, May, September, October, and November, in which typical days are mostly <a href="/wiki/Overcast" title="Overcast">overcast</a>, with low clouds and some winds, bringing maximum temperatures of 18&#160;&#176;C (64&#160;&#176;F) and lows of 7&#160;&#176;C (45&#160;&#176;F).\n</p><p><br/>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n<caption>Climate data for National Meteorological class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weather_Atlas_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weather_Atlas-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_layout_and_nomenclature">Urban layout and nomenclature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Urban layout and nomenclature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="909" data-file-width="721" decoding="async" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png/220px-How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png/330px-How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png/440px-How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Street arrangement of Bogot&#225; based on the Cartesian coordinate system: North is to the right</div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225; has 20 localities, or districts, forming an extensive network of neighborhoods. Areas of higher economic status tend to be located in the north, close to the Eastern Hills in the districts of <a href="/wiki/Chapinero" title="Chapinero">Chapinero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usaqu%C3%A9n" title="Usaqu&#233;n">Usaqu&#233;n</a> and the east of <a href="/wiki/Suba,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Suba, Bogot&#225;">Suba</a>. The lower middle class inhabit the central, western and northwestern parts of the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The working-class neighborhoods are located in the south, some of them <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanty_towns" title="Shanty towns">squatter areas</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The urban layout in the center of the city is based on the focal point of a square or plaza, typical of Spanish-founded settlements, but the layout gradually becomes more modern in outlying neighborhoods. The types of roads are classified as <i>Calles</i> (streets), which run from west to east horizontally, with street numbers increasing towards the north, and also towards the south (with the suffix "Sur") from Calle 0 down south. <i>Carreras</i> (roads) run from north to south vertically, with numbering increasing from east to west. (with the suffix "Este" for roads east of Carrera 0). At the southeast of the city, the addresses are logically <i>sur-este</i>. Other types of roads more common in newer parts of the city may be termed <i>Eje</i> (Axis), <i>Diagonal</i> or <i>Transversal</i>.\nThe numbering system for street addresses recently changed, and numbers are assigned according to street rank from main avenues to smaller avenues and local streets. Some of Bogot&#225;\'s main roads, which also go by a proper name in addition to a number, are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Norte-Quito-Sur or NQS (North Quito South Avenue, from 9th Rd at north following railway to 30th Rd, or Quito City Avenue, and Southern Highway)</li>\n<li>Autopista Norte-Avenida Caracas (Northern Highway, or 45th Rd, joined to Caracas Avenue, or 14th Rd)</li>\n<li>Avenida Circunvalar (or 1st Rd)</li>\n<li>Avenida Suba (60th transversal from 100th St the Suba Hills; 145th St from Suba Hills westward)</li>\n<li>Avenida El Dorado (El Dorado Avenue, or 26th St)</li>\n<li>Avenida de las Am&#233;ricas (Avenue of the Americas, from 34th street at east to 6th street at west)</li>\n<li>Avenida Primero de Mayo (May First Avenue, or 22nd St South)</li>\n<li>Avenida Ciudad de Cali (Cali City Avenue, or 86th Rd)</li>\n<li>Avenida Boyac&#225; (Boyac&#225; Avenue, or 72nd Rd)</li>\n<li>Autopista Sur (Southern Highway)</li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Localities_.28districts.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Localities_(districts)">Localities (districts)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Localities (districts)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable floatleft">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>Population of Bogot&#225; by year\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><style
