solid #bbbbbb">6,840,116</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+9.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2010</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">7,743,785</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+13.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2016</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">9,854,722</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+27.3%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The largest and most populous city in Colombia, Bogot&#225; had 6,778,691 inhabitants within the city\'s limits (2005 census),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005_Census_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-2005_Census-9">[9]</a></sup> with a population density of approximately 4,310 inhabitants per square kilometer. Only 15,810 people are located in rural areas of Capital District. 47.5% of the population are male and 52.5% women.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_(Medium_Variant).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="863" data-file-width="1576" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png/220px-Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png/330px-Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png/440px-Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_(Medium_Variant).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bogot&#225; Future Population (Medium Variant)</div></div></div>\n<p>In Bogot&#225;, as in the rest of the country, urbanization has accelerated due to industrialization as well as complex political and social reasons such as poverty and violence, which led to migration from rural to urban areas throughout the twentieth and twenty-first centuries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A dramatic example of this is the number of displaced people who have arrived in Bogot&#225; due to the internal armed conflict.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Some estimates show that Bogot&#225;\'s <a href="/wiki/Floating_population" title="Floating population">floating population</a> may be as high as 4 million people, most of them being migrant workers from other departments and displaced people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The majority of the displaced population lives in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciudad_Bol%C3%ADvar_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Ciudad Bol&#237;var (Bogot&#225;)">Ciudad Bol&#237;var</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kennedy_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Kennedy (Bogot&#225;)">Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usme" title="Usme">Usme</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosa_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Bosa (Bogot&#225;)">Bosa</a> sections.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The ethnic composition of the city\'s population includes minorities of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Colombian" title="Afro-Colombian">Afro-Colombian</a> people (1.5%), and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">Indigenous Amerindians</a> (0.2%); 98.27% of the population has no ethnic affiliation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> but are <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a> and whites.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bogot&#225; has gone to great lengths to change its formerly notorious crime rate and its image with increasing success after being considered in the 1990s to be one of the most violent cities in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 1993 there were 4,352 murders at a rate of 81 per 100,000 people;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> in 2007 Bogot&#225; suffered 1,401 murders at a rate of 20 per 100,000 inhabitants, and had a further reduction to 14 per 100,000 inhabitants in 2017 (the lowest since 1979).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> This success was mainly the result of a participatory and integrated security policy; "Comunidad Segura", that was first adopted in 1995 and continues to be enforced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> 1.2 percent of street addresses account for 99 percent of homicides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Bogot&#225; is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Republic of Colombia</a>, and houses the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Colombia" title="Congress of Colombia">Congress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_of_Colombia" title="Supreme Court of Justice of Colombia">Supreme Court of Justice</a> and the center of the executive administration as well as the residence of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Colombia" title="President of Colombia">President</a> (<a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o" title="Casa de Nari&#241;o">Casa de Nari&#241;o</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> These buildings, along with the Office of the Mayor, the Lievano Palace (Palacio Li&#233;vano), are located within a few meters from each other on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bol&#237;var Square">Bol&#237;var Square</a> (Plaza de Bol&#237;var). The square is located in the city\'s historical center, <a href="/wiki/La_Candelaria" title="La Candelaria">La Candelaria</a>, which features architecture in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_style" title="Spanish Colonial style">Spanish Colonial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Baroque_architecture" title="Spanish Baroque architecture">Spanish Baroque</a> styles.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="List of mayors of Bogot&#225;">Mayor of Bogot&#225;</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_City_Council" title="Bogot&#225; City Council">City Council</a> &#8211; both elected by popular vote &#8211; are responsible for city administration. In 2015 <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa" title="Enrique Pe&#241;alosa">Enrique Pe&#241;alosa</a> was elected Mayor; his term runs from 2016 to 2019.\n</p><p>The city is divided into 20 localities: <a href="/wiki/Usaqu%C3%A9n" title="Usaqu&#233;n">Usaqu&#233;n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chapinero" title="Chapinero">Chapinero</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Santa Fe (Bogot&#225;)">Santa Fe</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="San Crist&#243;bal (Bogot&#225;)">San Crist&#243;bal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usme" title="Usme">Usme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunjuelito" title="Tunjuelito">Tunjuelito</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosa_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Bosa (Bogot&#225;)">Bosa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kennedy_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Kennedy (Bogot&#225;)">Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fontib%C3%B3n" title="Fontib&#243;n">Fontib&#243;n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engativ%C3%A1" title="Engativ&#225;">Engativ&#225;</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suba_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Suba (Bogot&#225;)">Suba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrios_Unidos" title="Barrios Unidos">Barrios Unidos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teusaquillo" title="Teusaquillo">Teusaquillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_M%C3%A1rtires" title="Los M&#225;rtires">Los M&#225;rtires</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antonio_Nari%C3%B1o_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Antonio Nari&#241;o (Bogot&#225;)">Antonio Nari&#241;o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puente_Aranda" title="Puente Aranda">Puente Aranda</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Candelaria" title="La Candelaria">La Candelaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Uribe_Uribe,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Rafael Uribe Uribe, Bogot&#225;">Rafael Uribe Uribe</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciudad_Bol%C3%ADvar_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Ciudad Bol&#237;var (Bogot&#225;)">Ciudad Bol&#237;var</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumapaz_(Bogot%C3%A1)" title="Sumapaz (Bogot&#225;)">Sumapaz</a>.\n</p><p>Each of the 20 localities is governed by an administrative board elected by popular vote, made up of no fewer than seven members. The Mayor designates local mayors from candidates nominated by the respective administrative board.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="598" data-file-width="2335" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/800px-Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/1200px-Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/1600px-Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panorama of the Centro Internacional (International Centre) of Bogot&#225;</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225; is the main economic and industrial center of Colombia.\nThe Colombian government fosters the import of capital goods, Bogot&#225; being one of the main destinations of these imports.\n</p><p>In 2016 the World Cities Study Group and Network (GaWC) from the United Kingdom ranked Bogot&#225; as an Alpha&#8722;World City in the World Cities Study Group\'s inventory, a high-ranking. Alpha and Alpha- cities are important world cities that link major economic regions into the world economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Travel &amp; Tourism\'s share of the city\'s overall GDP stands at 2.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Bogot&#225; is responsible for 56% of the tourism that arrives to Colombia and is home 1,423 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multinational_companies" title="Multinational companies">multinational companies</a>. Bogot&#225; also ranked highly as a global city where <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">business</a> is done and meetings are held. Bogot&#225; is a growing international meetings destination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BestCities_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-BestCities-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the last year, Bogot&#225; has won 50 major international events, with 12 more world-class events in progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BestCities_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-BestCities-47">[47]</a></sup> The 16th <a href="/wiki/World_Summit_of_Nobel_Peace_Laureates" title="World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates">World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates</a> took place from February 2 to 5, 2017 in Bogot&#225;, Colombia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/One_Young_World" title="One Young World">One Young World</a> is the preeminent global forum for young leaders aged 18&#8211;30. Bogot&#225;, Colombia is the host city for Summit 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andino,_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3982" data-file-width="2986" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG/220px-Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG/330px-Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG/440px-Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andino,_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Centro_Andino" title="Centro Andino">Centro Andino</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The hotels in the historical center of La Candelaria and its surrounding areas cater to lovers of culture and the arts. This area also has the bulk of hostels in the city as well. In La Candelaria, there are many museums, including the <a href="/wiki/Botero_Museum" title="Botero Museum">Botero Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Gold Museum, Bogot&#225;">Gold Museum</a>. Close to La Candelaria is the Cerro <a href="/wiki/Monserrate" title="Monserrate">Monserrate</a>, which you can reach by cable car or funicular. The hotels located near Ciudad Salitre are intended for visitors who make short stops in Bogot&#225; and near <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a>.\n</p><p>Important landmarks and tourist stops in Bogot&#225; include the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Botanical_Garden" title="Bogot&#225; Botanical Garden">botanical garden Jos&#233; Celestino Mutis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Quinta_de_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Quinta de Bol&#237;var">Quinta de Bol&#237;var</a>, the national observatory, the <a href="/wiki/Planetarium_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Planetarium of Bogot&#225;">planetarium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maloka_Museum" title="Maloka Museum">Maloka</a>, the Colpatria observation point, the observation point of <a href="/wiki/La_Calera,_Cundinamarca" title="La Calera, Cundinamarca">La Calera</a>, the monument of the American flags, and La Candelaria (the historical district of the city). There is also Usaquen, a colonial landmark where brunch and flea market on Sundays is a traditional activity. The city has numerous green parks and amusement parks like Salitre Magico or Mundo Aventura.\n</p><p>Green areas surrounding Bogota are perfect locations for eco-tourism and hiking activities, in the eastern mountains of the city, just a few minutes walking from main roads, there are Quebrada La vieja and Chapinero Waterfalls, two of many green spots for sightseeing and tourism with clean air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are also several areas of the city where fine restaurants can be found. The G Zone, the T Zone, and La Macarena are well known for their gastronomic offerings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the 2000s, major hotel chains have established in the city. Bogota has a great cultural diversity, coming from different regions of the country, which allows the tourist to know the multiculturalism of the country without the need to travel to other cities, this includes gastronomy and different festivals.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 115.33333333333px"><div style="width: 115.33333333333px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 113.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Santuario_de_Monserrate,_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1173" class="gallerytext">\n<p>Maloka\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping_malls">Shopping malls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Shopping malls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_%281%29.jpg/220px-CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_%281%29.jpg/330px-CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_%281%29.jpg/440px-CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CC_Parque_La_Colina_Bogot%C3%A1_N_sep_2017_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parque La Colina Shopping Mall</div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225;\'s economy has been significantly boosted due to new shopping malls built within the last few years. As of  December&#160;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, over 160 new malls are planned in addition to the existing 100 malls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Notable malls include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Centro_Andino" title="Centro Andino">Centro Andino</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Centro_Mayor" title="Centro Mayor">Centro Mayor</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centro_Comercial_Santafe" title="Centro Comercial Santafe">Santaf&#233;</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gran_Estaci%C3%B3n" title="Gran Estaci&#243;n">Gran Estaci&#243;n</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portal_de_la_80" title="Portal de la 80">Portal de la 80</a></li>\n<li><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centro_comercial_Tit%C3%A1n_Plaza" title="es:Centro comercial Tit&#225;n Plaza">Tit&#225;n Plaza</a></li>\n<li><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centro_Comercial_Calima" title="es:Centro Comercial Calima">Calima</a></li>\n<li><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centro_Comercial_Atlantis_Plaza" title="es:Centro Comercial Atlantis Plaza">Atlantis Plaza</a></li>\n<li><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicentro" title="es:Unicentro">Unicentro</a></li>\n<li><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centro_Comercial_Hayuelos" title="es:Centro Comercial Hayuelos">Hayuelos</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Bogota is home to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Template:Bogot%C3%A1_TV" title="Template:Bogot&#225; TV">several television stations</a> like <a href="/wiki/Canal_Capital" title="Canal Capital">Canal Capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citytv_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Citytv Bogot&#225;">Citytv</a> which are local stations, <a href="/wiki/Canal_13_(Colombia)" title="Canal 13 (Colombia)">Canal 13</a> is a regional station, and is home to the national channels <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caracol_TV" title="Caracol TV">Caracol TV</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RCN_TV" title="RCN TV">RCN TV</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canal_Uno_(Colombia)" title="Canal Uno (Colombia)">Canal Uno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canal_Institucional" title="Canal Institucional">Canal Institucional</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%B1al_Colombia" title="Se&#241;al Colombia">Se&#241;al Colombia</a>. It has multiple satellite television services like <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica" title="Telef&#243;nica">Telef&#243;nica</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Claro_Americas" title="Claro Americas">Claro</a> and <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a> and several satellite dishes which offer hundreds of international channels, plus several exclusive channels for Bogot&#225;.\n</p><p>In Bogota, all the major radio networks in the country are available, in both AM and FM; 70% of the FM stations offer <a href="/wiki/Radio_Data_System" title="Radio Data System">RDS service</a>.\nThere are several newspapers, including <i><a href="/wiki/El_Tiempo_(Colombia)" title="El Tiempo (Colombia)">El Tiempo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Espectador" title="El Espectador">El Espectador</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_Siglo" title="El Nuevo Siglo">El Nuevo Siglo</a></i>, plus economical dailies La Rep&#250;blica<i> and </i>Portafolio<i>, tabloids </i>El Espacio<i>, </i>Q\'Hubo<i>, and </i>Extra<i>. Bogot&#225; also offers three free newspapers, two Spanish, ADN and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publimetro" title="Publimetro">Publimetro</a>, and one English, The Bogota Post.</i>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2633" data-file-width="3511" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG/220px-Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG/330px-Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG/440px-Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An old house in the <a href="/wiki/Teusaquillo" title="Teusaquillo">Teusaquillo</a> locality, near downtown Bogot&#225; (<i>Estrato 4</i>)</div></div></div>\n<p>Energy and sewer bills are stratified based on the location of owner\'s residence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The system is the classification of the residential properties that should receive public services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estrato_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-estrato-56">[56]</a></sup> Although the system does not consider the income per person and the rules say that the residential real estate should stratify and not households.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Preguntas_frecuentes_estratificaci&#243;n_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Preguntas_frecuentes_estratificaci&#243;n-57">[57]</a></sup> All mayors should do the stratification of residential properties of their municipality or district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estrato_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-estrato-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bogot&#225;\'s social strata have been divided as follows and have been extensively used by the government as a reference to develop social welfare programs, statistical information and to some degree for the assignment of lands.\n</p>\n<ul><li>Estrato 1 (lowest)</li>\n<li>Estrato 2 (low)</li>\n<li>Estrato 3 (mid-low)</li>\n<li>Estrato 4 (mid-high)</li>\n<li>Estrato 5 (high)</li>\n<li>Estrato 6 (highest)</li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3229" data-file-width="2916" decoding="async" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png/220px-TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png/330px-TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png/440px-TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a> system.</div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225;\'s growth has placed a strain on its roads and highways, but since 1998 significant efforts to upgrade the infrastructure have been undertaken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Private car ownership forms a major part of the congestion, in addition to taxis, buses and commercial vehicles. Buses remain the main means of mass transit. There are two bus systems: the traditional system and the <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a>.\n</p><p>The traditional system runs a variety of bus types, operated by several companies on normal streets and avenues: <i>Bus</i> (large buses), <i>Buseta</i> (medium size buses) and <i>Colectivo</i> (vans or minivans). The bigger buses were divided into two categories: <i>Ejecutivo</i>, which was originally to be a deluxe service and was not to carry standing passengers, and <i>corriente</i> or normal service. Since May 2008, all buses run as <i>corriente</i> services. Bogot&#225; is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation_hub" title="Transportation hub">hub</a> for domestic and international bus routes. The Bogot&#225; terminal serves routes to most cities and towns in Colombia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and is the largest in the country. There is international service to Ecuador, Per&#250; and Venezuela.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a> system was created during <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa" title="Enrique Pe&#241;alosa">Enrique Pe&#241;alosa</a>\'s mayoral term,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and is a form of <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> that has been deployed as a measure to compensate for the lack of a subway or rail system. TransMilenio combines articulated buses that operate on dedicated bus roads (busways) and smaller buses (feeders) that operate in residential areas, bringing passengers to the main grid. TransMilenio\'s main routes are: Caracas Avenue, Northern Highway (<i>Autopista Norte</i>), 80th Street, Americas Avenue, Jim&#233;nez Avenue, and 30th Avenue (also referred to as <i>Norte Quito Sur</i> or <i>N.Q.S.</i> for short). Routes for Suba Avenue and Southern Highway (<i>Autopista Sur</i>), the southern leg of the 30th Avenue, were opened in April 2006. The third phase of the system will cover 7th Avenue, 10th Avenue, and 26th Street (or <i>Avenida El Dorado</i>). The system is planned to cover the entire city by 2030. Although the Transmilenio carries commuters to numerous corners of the city, it is more expensive (US$0.80 or 2300 COP) than any public transport, except taxis.\n</p><p>In addition to TransMilenio, the Pe&#241;alosa administration and voter-approved referenda helped to establish travel restrictions on cars with certain license plate numbers during peak hours called <a href="/wiki/Pico_y_placa" title="Pico y placa">Pico y placa</a>; 121 kilometres (75 miles) of <a href="/wiki/Ciclov%C3%ADa" title="Ciclov&#237;a">Ciclov&#237;a</a> on Sundays and major holidays; a massive system (376&#160;km (234&#160;mi) as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) of bicycle paths and segregated lanes called <i><a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Bike_Paths_Network" title="Bogot&#225;\'s Bike Paths Network">ciclorrutas</a></i>; and the removal of thousands of parking spots in an attempt to make roads more pedestrian-friendly and discourage car use. <i>Ciclorrutas</i> is one of the most extensive dedicated bike path networks of any city in the world, with a total extension of 376 kilometres (234 miles). It extends from the north of the city, 170th Street, to the south, 27th Street, and from <a href="/wiki/Monserrate" title="Monserrate">Monserrate</a> on the east to the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_River" title="Bogot&#225; River">Bogot&#225; River</a> on the west. The <i>ciclorruta</i> was started by the 1995&#8211;1998 <a href="/wiki/Antanas_Mockus" title="Antanas Mockus">Antanas Mockus</a> administration with a few kilometers, and considerably extended afterwards with the development of a Bicycle Master Plan and the addition of paths hundreds of kilometers in extent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Since the construction of the <i>ciclorruta</i> bicycle use in the city has increased, and a car free week was introduced in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greenblog_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-greenblog-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Articulado_de_Transmilenio_en_el_Eje_Ambiental.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2723" data-file-width="3631" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Articulado_de_Transmilenio_en_el_Eje_Ambiental.JPG/480px-Articulado_de_Transmilenio_en_el_Eje_Ambiental.JPG 2x" width="160"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trancon_Autonorte.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2576" decoding="async" (Autopista Norte)\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2741" data-file-width="3795" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/220px-Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/330px-Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/440px-Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225;\'s main airport is <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a>, with an approximate area of 6.9&#160;km&#178; located west of the city\'s downtown in the <a href="/wiki/Fontib%C3%B3n" title="Fontib&#243;n">Fontib&#243;n</a> Locality. It is the third most important airport in Latin America after <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport" title="Mexico City International Airport">Mexico City International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo%E2%80%93Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="S&#227;o Paulo&#8211;Guarulhos International Airport">S&#227;o Paulo&#8211;Guarulhos International Airport</a> and it is the most important airport in Colombia. Construction of the airport was ordered by <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_Rojas_Pinilla" title="Gustavo Rojas Pinilla">Gustavo Rojas Pinilla</a> (19th President of Colombia) in 1955 to replace the <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeropuerto_de_Techo" title="es:Aeropuerto de Techo">Aeropuerto de Techo</a>. Due to its central location in Colombia and in Latin America, it is a hub for Colombia\'s Flagship Carrier <a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines_Colombia" title="Copa Airlines Colombia">Copa Airlines Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/LATAM_Colombia" title="LATAM Colombia">LATAM Colombia</a>. It is also serviced by a number of international airlines including American, Delta, United, Air France, KLM, Turkish Airlines, Jet Blue, and Lufthansa. The national airport has begun to take more responsibility due to the congestion at the international airport. In response to the high demand of approximately 27 Million passengers per year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> a new airport, El Dorado II, is planned to be built by 2021, to help alleviate traffic at the main airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A secondary airport, <a href="/wiki/Military_Transport_Air_Command_(Colombian_Air_Force)" title="Military Transport Air Command (Colombian Air Force)">CATAM</a>, serves as a base for Military and Police Aviation. This airport, which uses the runways of El Dorado will eventually move to Madrid, a nearby town in the region of Cundinamarca, leaving further space to expand El Dorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Guaymaral_Airport" title="Guaymaral Airport">Guaymaral Airport</a> is another small airport located in the northern boundaries of Bogota. It is used mainly for private aviation activities.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_and_suburban_railways">Urban and suburban railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Urban and suburban railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Metro" title="Bogot&#225; Metro">Bogot&#225; Metro</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tramways_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Tramways of Bogot&#225;">Tramways of Bogot&#225;</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Savannah_Railway" title="Bogot&#225;\'s Savannah Railway">Bogot&#225;\'s Savannah Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Train_for_the_vicinities_of_the_city_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Train for the vicinities of the city of Bogot&#225;">Train for the vicinities of the city of Bogot&#225;</a></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225; has little railway transit infrastructure, following the collapse of the tram network, although a number of plans hope to change that. The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Metro" title="Bogot&#225; Metro">Bogot&#225; Metro</a> has been pushed forward by two successive governments, and proponents hope that construction will soon begin. Plans to construct railways in and out of the city, replacing defunct routes, have been delayed due to the pressing need for transport within the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle_infrastructure">Bicycle infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bicycle infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Bike_Paths_Network" title="Bogot&#225;\'s Bike Paths Network">Bogot&#225;\'s Bike Paths Network</a></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225; is the Colombian city with the most extensive and comprehensive network of bike paths. Bogot&#225;\'s bike paths network or Ciclorutas de Bogot&#225; in Spanish, designed and built during the administration of Mayors <a href="/wiki/Antanas_Mockus" title="Antanas Mockus">Antanas Mockus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa" title="Enrique Pe&#241;alosa">Enrique Pe&#241;alosa</a>, is also one of the most extensive in the world and the most extensive in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The network is integrated with the <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a> bus system which has bicycle parking facilities.\n</p><p>Bogota implemented a healthy habit called "Ciclovia" where principal highways are closed from 7:00&#160;a.m. until 2:00 pm on Sundays and public holidays; therefore, the People ride their bikes to enjoy the city as well as exercise. In the same way just on December the same activity is carried out in the night, there are some special activities such as fireworks, street theater performances, and street food just to mention a few.\n</p><p>Since the 4th of April 2016 the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carrera_11&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carrera 11 (page does not exist)">carrera 11</a> has been reduced from four to three car lanes and a new bike lane (<i>cicloruta</i>) has been inaugurated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tramway">Tramway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tramway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 25 December 1884, the first tramway pulled by mules was inaugurated and covered the route from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bol&#237;var Square">Plaza de Bol&#237;var</a> to Chapinero,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PorupRaub2009_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-PorupRaub2009-69">[69]</a></sup> and in 1892, the line connecting Plaza de Bol&#237;var and La Sabana Station started operating. The tramway ran over wooden rails and was easily derailed, so steel rails imported from England were eventually installed. In 1894, a tramway car ran the Bogot&#225;&#8211;Chapinero line every 20 minutes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The tram system eventually grew to cover most of the city and its surrounding suburbs. But during the <a href="/wiki/Bogotazo" title="Bogotazo">Bogotazo</a> riots of 1948, the system suffered heavy damage and was forced to close. The economic effects of the <a href="/wiki/La_Violencia" title="La Violencia">subsequent civil war</a> that followed prevented the damage from being repaired. Parts of the system continued to operate in a reduced state until 1951, when they were replaced by buses. Most of the streetcar tracks were eventually paved over, but exposed tracks can still be seen on many of the older roads of the city, especially downtown and in the <a href="/wiki/La_Candelaria" title="La Candelaria">La Candelaria</a> area, although it has been about 70 years<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> since any vehicles have run on them.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bogota_public_transportation_statistics">Bogota public transportation statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Bogota public transportation statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Bogota, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 97 min. 32% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 20 min, while 40% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 8&#160;km, while 16% travel for over 12&#160;km in a single direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Bogot%C3%A1" title="List of universities in Bogot&#225;">List of universities in Bogot&#225;</a></div>\n<p>Known as the Athens of South America,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Bogot&#225; has an extensive educational system of both primary and secondary schools and colleges. Due to the constant migration of people into the nation\'s capital, the availability of quotas for access to education offered by the State free of charge is often insufficient. The city also has a diverse system of colleges and private schools.\n</p><p>There are a number of universities, both public and private. In 2002, there were a total of 114 higher education institutions; in Bogot&#225; there are several universities, most partially or fully accredited by the NAC (National Accreditation Council): <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia" title="National University of Colombia">National University of Colombia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_the_Andes,_Colombia" title="University of the Andes, Colombia">University of the Andes, Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/District_University_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="District University of Bogot&#225;">District University of Bogot&#225;</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University,_Colombia" title="La Salle University, Colombia">La Salle University, Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_La_Sabana" title="University of La Sabana">University of La Sabana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Xavierian_University" title="Pontifical Xavierian University">Pontifical Xavierian University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary_University" title="Our Lady of the Rosary University">Our Lady of the Rosary University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Externado_de_Colombia" title="Universidad Externado de Colombia">Universidad Externado de Colombia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_University_Nueva_Granada" title="Military University Nueva Granada">Military University Nueva Granada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_University_(Colombia)" title="Central University (Colombia)">Central University, Colombia</a>,<a href="/wiki/University_of_America" title="University of America">University of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Arboleda_University" title="Sergio Arboleda University">Sergio Arboleda University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Tadeo_Lozano_University" title="Jorge Tadeo Lozano University">Jorge Tadeo Lozano University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilot_University_of_Colombia" title="Pilot University of Colombia">Pilot University of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_University_of_Colombia" title="Catholic University of Colombia">Catholic University of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas_Aquinas_University" title="Saint Thomas Aquinas University">Saint Thomas Aquinas University</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Pedagogic_University_(Colombia)" title="National Pedagogic University (Colombia)">Universidad Pedag&#243;gica Nacional</a>.\n</p><p>The city has a University City at the National University of Colombia campus located in the traditional sector Teusaquillo. It is the largest campus in Colombia and one of the largest in Latin America.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional centre">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div style="width: 235px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fray_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_Torres.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3000" Claustro" at the <a href="/wiki/Del_Rosario_University" title="Del Rosario University">Del Rosario University</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div of Colombia</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div style="width: 235px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG/400px-Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Centro &#193;tico at <a style="width: 235px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Universidad_de_los_Andes_(3326108271).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg/200px-Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg" class="gallerytext">\n<p>Mario Laserna building in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Los_Andes_(Colombia)" title="University of Los Andes (Colombia)">University of the Andes</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg/220px-Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg/330px-Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg/440px-Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ciclov%C3%ADa" title="Ciclov&#237;a">Ciclov&#237;a</a> in Bogot&#225;</div></div></div>\n<p>Bogot&#225; has many cultural venues including 58 museums, 62 art galleries, 33 library networks, 45 stage theaters, 75 sports and attraction parks, and over 150 national monuments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Many of these are renowned globally such as:\nThe <a href="/wiki/Luis_%C3%81ngel_Arango_Library" title="Luis &#193;ngel Arango Library">Luis &#193;ngel Arango Library</a>, the most important in the region<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2015)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> which receives well over 6 million visitors a year;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Colombian_National_Museum" title="Colombian National Museum">Colombian National Museum</a>, one of the oldest in the Americas, dating back to 1823;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>\nThe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Theater_Festival" title="Ibero-American Theater Festival">Ibero-American Theater Festival</a>, largest of its kind in the world, receives 2 million attendees enjoying over 450 performances across theaters and off the street;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Philharmonic" title="Bogot&#225; Philharmonic">Bogot&#225; Philharmonic</a> is the most important<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2015)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Symphony_orchestra" title="Symphony orchestra">symphony orchestra</a> in Colombia, with over 100 musicians and 140 performances a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The city has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network" title="Creative Cities Network">UNESCO Creative Cities Network</a> in the category of music since March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Crist&#243;bal Col&#243;n Theater, the country\'s oldest Opera House, opened in 1892. It is home to the National Symphony Association\'s major act, the <a href="/wiki/National_Symphony_Orchestra_of_Colombia" title="National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia">National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rock_al_Parque" title="Rock al Parque">Rock al Parque</a> or Rock at the Park is an open air rock music festival. Recurring annually, it gathers over 320,000 music fans who can enjoy over 60 band performances for free during three days a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The series have been so successful during its 15 years of operation that the city has replicated the initiative for other music genres, resulting in other recent festivals like Salsa at the Park, Hip Hop at the Park, Ballet at the Park, Opera at the Park, and Jazz at the Park.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Awards_Colombia" title="Kids\' Choice Awards Colombia">Kids\' Choice Awards Colombia</a>, are the most important<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2015)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> awards given in the city by <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> and the first ceremony was given in 2014 by the singer <a href="/wiki/Maluma_(singer)" title="Maluma (singer)">Maluma</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Corferias" title="Corferias">Corferias</a> the ceremony has been the home of shows given by artists like <a href="/wiki/Austin_Mahone" title="Austin Mahone">Austin Mahone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pe%C3%B1a" title="Carlos Pe&#241;a">Carlos Pe&#241;a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Tetto" title="Don Tetto">Don Tetto</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Riva_(singer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Riva (singer) (page does not exist)">Riva</a> among others.\n</p><p>Bogot&#225; has worked in recent years to position itself as leader in cultural offerings in South America, and it is increasingly being recognized worldwide as a hub in the region for the development of the arts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\nIn 2007, Bogot&#225; was awarded the title of Cultural Capital of <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">Ibero-America</a> by the UCCI (<a href="/wiki/Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities" title="Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities">Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities</a>), and it became the only city to have received the recognition twice, after being awarded for the first time in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_history">Cultural history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cultural history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bogot&#225; gave the Spanish-speaking world <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Asunci%C3%B3n_Silva" title="Jos&#233; Asunci&#243;n Silva">Jos&#233; Asunci&#243;n Silva</a> (1865&#8211;1896), <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">Modernism</a> pioneer. His poetic work in the novel <i>De sobremesa</i> has a place in outstanding American literature. <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Pombo" title="Rafael Pombo">Rafael Pombo</a> (1833&#8211;1912) was an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_romanticism" title="American romanticism">American romanticism</a> poet who left a collection of fables essential part of children imagination and Colombian tradition.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5152" data-file-width="3864" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG/170px-Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG/255px-Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG/340px-Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/BD_Bacat%C3%A1" title="BD Bacat&#225;">BD Bacat&#225;</a>, under construction, will be the city\'s tallest building.</div></div></div>\n<p>The urban morphology and typology of colonial buildings in Bogot&#225; have been maintained since the late nineteenth century, long after the independence of Colombia (1810).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This persistence of the colonial setting is still visible, particularly in La Candelaria, the historical center of Bogot&#225;. Also kept up are the colonial houses of two stories, with courtyards, gabled roofs, ceramic tiles and balconies. In some cases, these balconies were enclosed with glass windows during the Republican period, a distinguishing feature of the architecture of the sector (for example, the House of Rafael Pombo).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>"Republican Architecture" was the style that prevailed between 1830 and 1930.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although there were attempts to consolidate a modern architectural language, the only examples seen are University City and White City at the National University of Colombia (constructed 1936 to 1939).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This work was developed by German architect <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Rother" title="Leopold Rother">Leopold Rother</a>, although architects of rationalist trends participated in the design of campus buildings. We also see in Bogotan architecture trends such as art deco, expressionism and organic architecture. This last trend was typified by Bogotan architects in the second half of the twentieth century such as <a href="/wiki/Rogelio_Salmona" title="Rogelio Salmona">Rogelio Salmona</a>.\n</p><p>Although renowned for its beautiful preservation of colonial architecture, there are also significant contemporary architecture examples found in the downtown and at the north of the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>In 2015 BD Bacat&#225; was inaugurated, surpassing the Colpatria Tower to become the tallest building of the city and of Colombia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The building its expected to be the beginning of the city\'s downtown renovation.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2951" data-file-width="3935" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/240px-Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/360px-Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/480px-Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 2x" width="160"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Santa Barbara business district\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casas_en_La_Merced,_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2373" data-file-width="3164" decoding="async" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Casas_en_La_Merced%2C_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/360px-Casas_en_La_Merced%2C_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Casas_en_La_Merced%2C_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/480px-Casas_en_La_Merced%2C_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 2x" width="160"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian architecture</a> in <a href="/wiki/Teusaquillo" title="Teusaquillo">Teusaquillo</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px Parque\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Santa_Maria.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/La_Santa_Maria.JPG/240px-La_Santa_Maria.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/La_Santa_Maria.JPG/360px-La_Santa_Maria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/La_Santa_Maria.JPG/480px-La_Santa_Maria.JPG 2x" width="160"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Santa Maria <a href="/wiki/Bullring" title="Bullring">bullring</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_archives">Libraries and archives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Libraries and archives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2007 Bogot&#225; was named <a href="/wiki/World_Book_Capital" title="World Book Capital">World Book Capital</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Bogot&#225; is the first Latin American city to receive this recognition, and the second one in the Americas after <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>. It stood out in programs, the library network and the presence of organizations that, in a coordinated manner, are working to promote books and reading in the city. Several specific initiatives for the World Book Capital program have been undertaken with the commitment of groups, both public and private, engaged in the book sector.\n</p><p>The city is home to the Biblored, an institution which administers 16 small and four large public libraries (Biblioteca Virgilio Barco, Biblioteca El Tintal, Biblioteca El Tunal and Biblioteca Julio Mario Santodomingo). It also has six branches of the Library Network of the Family Compensation Fund Colsubsidio and libraries and documentation centers attached to institutions like the Museo Nacional de Colombia (specializing in old books, catalogs and art), Museum of Modern Art, the Alliance Fran&#231;aise, and the Centro Colombo Americano.\n</p><p>Another set of libraries are the new collaborative initiatives between the state, city and international agencies. Examples are the Cultural Center Gabriel Garc&#237;a Marquez, custom designed by the Fondo de Cultura Economica in Mexico, and the Spanish Cultural Center, which will begin construction with public funds and of the Spanish government in downtown Bogot&#225;.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Colombia" title="National Library of Colombia">National Library of Colombia</a> (1777), a dependence of the Ministry of Culture and the Biblioteca Luis Angel Arango (1958), a dependence of the Bank of the Republic are the two largest public libraries in the city. The first is the repository of more than two million volumes, with an important collection of ancient books. The latter has almost two million volumes, and with 45,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (480,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Square_foot" title="Square foot">sq&#160;ft</a>) in size, it hosts 10,000 visitors a day; the Library Alfonso Palacio Rudas is also a dependence of the Bank of the Republic, and is located at the north of the city, with about 50,000 volumes. Other large public libraries are the Library of Congress in Colombia (with 100,000 volumes), of the Instituto Caro y Cuervo (with nearly 200,000 volumes, the largest Latin American library in Philology and Linguistics), the Library of the Academy of History The Library of the Academy of Language, the Library of the Colombian Institute of Anthropology and History ICANH, and many university libraries.\n</p><p>Bogot&#225; is home to historical records housed in the General National Archive, a collection of about 60 million documents, one of the largest repositories of primary historical sources in Latin America. Bogot&#225; is also home to the Musical Archive of the Cathedral of Bogot&#225; (with thousands of books and choral song-colonial period), the Archdiocesan Archive, the Archive of the Conciliar Seminary of Bogot&#225;, the Archive History National University of Colombia and the Archive of the Mint in Bogot&#225;, under the Bank of the Republic.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image"
